1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5. Pro: Remaining in the EU would exacerbate political instability.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.1. Con: Disarray in British politics isn't necessarily negative, as it may call into question the existing system and lead to calls for reform.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.1.1. Pro: This reform could include rethinking the two \(three\) party system, and the need for proportionality voting. If Brexit does not work out, it may become clear that having two parties vying for votes by diametrically opposing each other does not lead to successful policies. It may indicate the need for broader electoral support, and coalitions between parties.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.2. Pro: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.4.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3. Con: A hard Brexit threatens the constitutional set-up of the United Kingdom and its associated territories, more so than overturning the referendum result and staying in the EU.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.1. Con: A hard Brexit is simply an excuse used by people who wanted to threaten the unity of the United Kingdom before the Brexit referendum was even a glimmer in David Cameron's eye.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.1.1. Pro: Sinn Fein has [long been calling for reunification](http://www.firstdail.com/?page_id=208) of the island of Ireland since well before the EU referendum.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.1.2. Pro: The SNP has long [been calling for](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014) secession of Scotland.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.1.3. Pro: Welsh nationalists have [long been calling for](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Welsh_nationalism) secession of Wales.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.1.4. Con: Brexit gives weight to nationalist political parties who will insist that England is forcing its own agenda on Scotland, Wales and Northern Ireland.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2. Pro: A hard Brexit could trigger a second independence referendum within Scotland.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2.1. Con: This could happen anyway. All voters in the first Scottish referendum were aware there was an upcoming referendum on EU membership and so this was factored in to voting decisions.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2.1.1. Con: The campaign for Scotland remaining in the UK stated:["What is process for removing our EU citizenship? Voting yes."](https://twitter.com/uk_together/status/506899714923843584?lang=en) This suggests voters did not factor this in to their decision. In fact, it claimed that their desire to stay in the EU was a reason to vote for the Union, whereas today they would more likely to see independence as the best route to staying in the EU.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2.2. Pro: If Brexit proves to harm the UK economy as many people predict, then it could persuade enough people in Scotland to leave the UK. During the original Scottish Independence Referendum, the Better Together website said: “Scotland enjoys membership of the EU because of our membership of the UK and if we no longer are members of the UK then it follows that we are no longer part of the EU.” [Link](https://www.snp.org/broken_promises_by_tories_and_no_campaign_since_indyref). Scots who voted to stay in the UK for continued EU membership now feel cheated as a result of Brexit.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2.3. Con: The SNP is unlikely to hold a second independence referendum as only [46%](https://www.scotsman.com/news/politics/what-the-latest-polls-tell-us-about-scottish-independence-1-4636493) of Scots support it.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2.3.1. Pro: It is highly unlikely that the SNP will choose to call for a second referendum unless they're certain to win, as a loss would be a devastating blow to their party.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2.3.2. Pro: The Scottish National Party does not have an [established timeframe](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2017/jun/27/nicola-sturgeon-shelves-second-independence-referendum) for a second referendum, showing no current intention to push for one.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2.4. Pro: First Minister of Scotland Nicola Sturgeon claims it is ["likely"](http://www.bbc.com/news/uk-scotland-40415457) that a referendum will take place before 2021.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2.4.1. Pro: The Scottish Government were elected on a manifesto that said they would seek to hold another referendum in the event of a vote for Brexit. They won a majority of seats at UK and Scottish level on this manifesto.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2.4.2. Con: It is in the interests of the leader of the Scottish National Party to claim a second referendum will take place, as it will keep her hard nationalist base happy. Her statements should not be read as accurate predictions.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2.4.3. Con: It is impossible for there to be another Independence Referendum without approval from the Prime Minister under [Section 30 of the Scotland Act](https://inews.co.uk/news/politics/section-30-scotland-act-1998-important/).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.2.5. Pro: Scotland voted overwhelmingly to stay within the European Union, a margin of [62% to 38%](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/politics/eu_referendum/results), with every single electorate returning a majority in favour of Remain.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.3. Con: Strong independence movements exist within the European Union, as illustrated by the recent [crisis in Catalonia](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-41584864). There's no reason to believe that remaining in the EU would protect the UK from secession.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.3.1. Con: Calatonian independence movement is [pro EU](https://frontnews.eu/news/en/13858/Catalonia-wants-to-stay-in-European-Union-president-of-Catalan-Government). In the UK Northern Ireland independence movement [wants to get independence](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/home-news/northern-ireland-support-join-irish-republic-eu-hard-brexit-poll-lucidtalk-a8098531.html) mainly because after Brexit the free border with Ireland will be closed, resulting in [huge damages](https://www.belfasttelegraph.co.uk/business/brexit/predicted-brexit-hit-to-northern-ireland-economy-reality-check-for-may-and-dup-36580101.html) for the Northern Ireland economy and in a hard divison of the island.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.3.1.1. Pro: The EU contributed to [8.4%](http://www.paxetbellum.org/2017/03/21/could-brexit-summon-the-ghosts-of-the-troubles/) of the Northern Irish GDP through financial aid. Without its support the Northern Irish economy will suffer.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.3.1.1.1. Con: This was the UK's money to begin with. The UK government has [already committed](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/business/news/dup-deal-latest-how-much-extra-money-funding-theresa-may-conservative-tory-uk-taxpayers-a7809231.html) to very significant increases in NI funding.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.3.1.1.2. Con: This assumes a post Brexit UK will not be able to secure new lucrative trade opportunities, which is very much up for debate.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.3.1.1.3. Con: Westminster is likely to offer more financial support to plug the gap, both because of the [DUP's position](https://uk.reuters.com/article/uk-britain-politics-may/may-strikes-1-billion-deal-with-dup-to-prop-up-government-idUKKBN19H0H3) in Theresa May's government, and to ensure stability.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.3.2. Con: Ruling by example is good choice. It's difficult to claim union while breaking up bigger commitments in pro of equality in terms of rights and obligations
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.4. Pro: A hard Brexit threatens British sovereignty over Gibraltar \(a small territory [bordering Southern Spain](https://www.google.co.uk/maps/place/Gibraltar/\@36.218638,-5.4795662,9z/data=!4m5!3m4!1s0xd0cbf762714be35:0x384e25263600870f!8m2!3d36.140751!4d-5.353585)\).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.4.1. Con: A change to the status of Gibraltar would not alter the constitutional set-up of the UK, as Gibraltar is not part of the UK.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.4.1.1. Con: Gibraltar is part of the Overseas Territories of the UK, and therefore it affects the constitution of the UK by proxy.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.4.2. Con: Spain's primary route to bullying and threatening the people of Gibraltar is through its use of [veto](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/apr/07/will-the-uk-lose-gibraltar) in the EU. If there is no deal with the EU, Spain has nothing to veto. A soft Brexit is therefore much more threatening to Gibraltar.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.4.2.1. Con: Spain's veto applies to any future EU deals, and so while a no deal may leave Spain temporarily with nothing to veto, when the UK eventually makes a trade deal with the EU Spain will still be able to use it.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.4.3. Pro: Spain has been [awarded a veto](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/apr/07/will-the-uk-lose-gibraltar) on all trade deals with Gibraltar in future EU negotiations. It could use this to strong-arm Gibraltar to accept Spanish sovereignty.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5. Pro: A hard Brexit would throw into disarray the constitutional arrangement between the Republic of Ireland and Northern Ireland, which represents a serious threat to the peace of the citizens of Northern Ireland.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.1. Con: There is no constitutional legal barrier to the UK leaving the EU. The constitutional arrangement between NI and the rest of the UK predates the EU.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.2. Con: The party which won 55% of NI seats in the 2017 general election campaign had a [manifesto committment to leave the EU](https://brexitcentral.com/dup-manifesto-said-brexit/), and to renege on this would throw into disarray the constitutional arrangement between the Republic of Ireland and Northern Ireland, which represents a serious threat to peace for the citizens of Northern Ireland.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.2.1. Con: Notwithstanding the percentage of seats won, this party represents a minority position \(25.7%\) 1.2% above the second placed party. [UK General election 2017 \(Northern Ireland\)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017_\(Northern_Ireland\))
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.2.2. Con: Manifesto commitments are often [dropped](https://www.theguardian.com/society/2017/may/22/theresa-may-u-turn-on-dementia-tax-cap-social-care-conservative-manifesto) by Governments when proved to be unpopular or unworkable.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3. Pro: A hard exit from the EU could call the [Good Friday Agreement](http://politicalcritique.org/world/uk/2017/what-would-a-hard-brexit-mean-for-ireland/) into question and could possibly cause a return to the violence and terror present in Northern Ireland during [The Troubles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Troubles).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.1. Pro: Violence has never fully ceased in Northern Ireland and so it would not be a large stretch for it to return to the way it was before the Good Friday Agreement.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.1.1. Pro: On Feb 2017 there was a [bomb explosion](https://m.belfasttelegraph.co.uk/news/northern-ireland/derry-bomb-culmore-device-at-police-officers-home-more-intricate-than-a-basic-pipe-bomb-35472857.html) at a police officer’s house in Derry/Londonderry. It is suspected that this was planned by violent dissident republicans.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.2. Con: There is nothing in the Good Friday Agreement that prohibits the UK leaving the EU.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.2.1. Con: The Good Friday Agreement makes references to both the UK and the Republic of Ireland being part of the EU as well as an open border. Creating a hard border would violate the terms of the agreement and hence would need to be rewritten with consent from both sides. History has proved this to be very difficult. [Good Friday Agreement](https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/the-belfast-agreement)
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.3. Pro: The Sinn Féin President, [Gerry Adams](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/brexit-northern-irealand-gerry-adams-sinn-fein-good-friday-agreement-peace-eu-a7539011.html), argued that Brexit will ‘destroy the Good Friday Agreement’, being at odds with consent for change, undermining its human rights elements and reinforcing the border.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.4. Pro: The Police Service of Northern Ireland has [observed](https://www.chathamhouse.org/publications/twt/brexit-s-threat-northern-ireland) that dissident Republicans and criminal gangs will also seek to tap into the smuggling opportunity presented by a customs border. This could lead to reorganization of old groups as well as new financial streams for them.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.5. Con: Irish Republicans currently [lack](https://www.chathamhouse.org/publications/twt/brexit-s-threat-northern-ireland) political leadership to organize violence.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.5.1. Con: While they lack a prominent leader this does not seem to be stifling growth. Republican clubs and societies – broadly supportive of armed violence against the British state and not directly controlled by the Sinn Féin leadership − are [increasingly active](https://www.chathamhouse.org/publications/twt/brexit-s-threat-northern-ireland) in border communities, drawing energy from the anger that has swelled in these areas since the Brexit vote.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.6. Con: The UK will no doubt have to [increase support for peace](https://www.chathamhouse.org/publications/twt/brexit-s-threat-northern-ireland) programs and negotiate a new border policy. But with sensible policies peace in Northern Ireland can be maintained.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.6.1. Con: A hard Brexit would lead to the return of an enforced border between Northern Ireland and The Republic of Ireland.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.6.1.1. Pro: The fact there are no customs checks on the border [is reliant on](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-42180074) Northern Ireland and The Republic of Ireland having the same food, animal welfare, environmental, and other standards. Without these, customs checks would be needed.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.6.1.2. Con: The border could be, in effect, [moved to the Irish Sea](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-42180074), leaving Northern Ireland effectively within the EU.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.6.1.2.1. Con: This would effectively allow Northern Ireland a "back door" into the EU market. In the context of a hard Brexit this would likely be unacceptable to the EU member states.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.6.1.2.2. Con: Both the UK government and the DUP in Northern Ireland have [ruled out](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-42180074) this option.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.6.1.2.2.1. Con: The UK government have ruled out membership of the single market and the customs union. They've ruled out a hard border across the island. They've ruled out a border down the Irish Sea. This is, for obvious reasons, a logically incoherent position. The UK will have no choice but to renege on one of these commitments.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.7. Pro: Brexit occurs at a time when[shifting demographics in Northern Ireland](https://www.newsletter.co.uk/news/catholic-population-set-to-dwarf-protestants-in-years-ahead-1-7872318) are tipping in favour of nationalists. Already, in the most recent elections, the unionist majority has disappeared. Within a decade, there will be a significant nationalist [majority in favour of unification](https://www.belfasttelegraph.co.uk/opinion/news-analysis/demographics-are-shifting-towards-a-united-ireland-we-must-have-a-plan-35865222.html). Tensions between communities are running high and there is truly the potential for a return to conflict and violence. Everything must be done to ensure the GFA is protected and a hard border across the island is avoided.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.8. Pro: Irish member of parliament [Neale Richmond](http://nationalpost.com/news/world/is-brexit-going-to-restart-the-troubles-in-northern-ireland) warned that border posts would be a “target for dissident paramilitaries.”
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.8.1. Con: The UK government has [repeatedly stated](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-northern-ireland-41365301) there will be no Irish border posts.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.8.1.1. Con: Stating something does not make it real. A stated desire for no border posts is a negotiating position, not a fact.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.4. Pro: The possibility of a no-deal Brexit has already [shifted the balance](https://www.independent.co.uk/author/mary-dejevsky) in Northern Ireland.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5. Pro: A hard Brexit could lead to a secession of Northern Ireland to rejoin the Republic of Ireland and the European Union.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5.1. Pro: The tightening of border controls, which would be necessary after a hard Brexit, will increase support for the succession of Northern Ireland.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.3.6.1.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5.2. Con: This could happen anyway independent of Brexit.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.1.1.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5.3. Pro: Northern Ireland voted to Remain in the EU by a [10% margin](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/politics/eu_referendum/results) \(55-45\).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5.4. Con: The Democratic Unionist Party, the [largest party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly) in the Northern Irish Assembly, is [opposed](http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/country_profiles/4172307.stm) to seccession.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5.4.1. Con: The politics of Ireland are incredibly volatile, there has not been a Government in Northern Ireland [since January 2017](https://www.economist.com/news/britain/21731338-belfasts-politicians-continue-bicker-brexit-talks-go-without-them-northern-ireland-hasnt) due to the collapse of power sharing. Therefore the continuation of the DUP as the major party in Northern Ireland is not guaranteed.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5.4.1.1. Pro: The Unionist Parties \([pro-union](http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/country_profiles/4172307.stm) with the UK\) hold only a [small plurality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly) over the Nationalist Parties \([pro-unification](http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/country_profiles/4172307.stm) with Southern Ireland\) in the Northern Irish Assembly.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5.5. Con: Even after the Brexit vote, support in Northern Ireland for reunification only stands at [22%](https://www.irishtimes.com/news/ireland/irish-news/sharp-rise-in-support-for-united-ireland-survey-reveals-1.2784882).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5.5.1. Con: While [22 per cent](https://www.irishtimes.com/news/ireland/irish-news/sharp-rise-in-support-for-united-ireland-survey-reveals-1.2784882?mode=amp) seems a low percentage, what is important is that it was a five-point increase in support for a United Ireland from 17 per cent in 2013. Since 2016 when this poll was taken support has continued to rise.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.5.5.1.1. Pro: In a [poll](http://foreignpolicy.com/2017/12/13/theresa-may-just-negotiated-away-the-united-kingdom/amp/?__twitter_impression=true) taken in December 2017 a majority in Northern Ireland \(51 percent\) supported unification under the Irish Republic to remain in the European Union in the event of a “hard” Brexit.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.6. Pro: Preventing a hard border between Northern Ireland and the Republic of Ireland could be [incompatible](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2018/02/06/brexit-bind-hard-border-ireland-could-unavoidable-uks-customs/) with leaving the Customs Union.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.6.1. Con: This is a solvable problem according to the British government and [the former Taoiseach \(Prime Minister\) of Ireland](https://www.irishtimes.com/news/politics/bertie-ahern-technology-and-turning-blind-eye-could-solve-brexit-border-issue-1.3306710).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.6.1.1. Pro: One possible solution that has been [mooted](https://www.irishtimes.com/news/politics/bertie-ahern-technology-and-turning-blind-eye-could-solve-brexit-border-issue-1.3306710?mode=amp) is to introduce technology to manage multinational trade while turning a blind eye to lower-level cross-frontier movement.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.6.1.1.1. Con: "Turning a blind eye" allows the movement of EU immigrants into the UK and vice versa. Brexit was claimed to be about taking back control of our borders. ROI/EU also has the right to controlled migration from the UK of both UK citizens and migrants we allow in too.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.3.5.6.1.2. Pro: If Britain leaves the EU common market a hard Irish border could be avoided if policies were implemented to separate Northern Ireland's market from the rest of the UK.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.4. Con: Domestic British politics will be in chaos now whatever happens.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.4.1. Pro: Given the narrow margin of victory, any course taken after the referendum was bound to throw British politics into chaos.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.4.2. Con: British politics would be even more thrown into chaos by a Hard Brexit, which would create [a shortage of food and medicine](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/brexit-no-deal-food-medicine-shortage-doomsday-armageddon-david-davis-a8381076.html).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.4.2.1. Con: The source above also has a government official saying: 'A significant amount of work and decision-making has gone into the no-deal plans, especially where it relates to ports, and we know that none of this would come to pass.'
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.4.2.1.1. Con: An example of "No deal planning" is the infamous "[Seabourne Ferries](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2019/jan/04/chris-grayling-brexit-pizza-ferry-company-zero-ships)" contract worth £14million granted to a company without ferries with their T&C copied off a takeaway menu. This can probably be assumed to be typical.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.5. Con: Fractured and irreconcilable differences over the EU is the cause of the failure of the Conservative Party, which is the [cause](https://www.ft.com/content/0dee56c0-fdfa-11e8-ac00-57a2a826423e) of the failure of uk politics and leaving will not address this issue.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.5.1. Pro: This failure started with the holding of the referendum, a decision made by David Cameron. It was not necessary. Politicians frequently break campaign promises because it's impractical not to when it's not practical to completely research an issue before the campaign and yet it's necessary to make a best guess on a wide variety of issues.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6. Pro: Refusing to enact the specific instructions from the electorate may lead to widespread civil disobedience, with negative consequences that dwarf any possible drawbacks from a hard Brexit.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.1. Pro: Perceived refusal by politicians to listen to voters has led to widespread and longstanding disruption in France through the [Yellow Vest movement.](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_vests_movement) Similar protests could become commonplace in the UK.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.1.1. Con: The [Yellow Vests movement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_vests_movement) does not appear to be primarily devoted to a failure of French politicians to listen to the voters. Rather its focus is on fuel prices and other mundane issues which boil down to a focus on money. Thus there are no lessons to be drawn regarding the effectiveness of their very different respective motivations.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.1.2. Con: Protesting against taxes is common, and does not indicate any increased likelihood of violent protests against a very different issue: a government ignoring a referendum decision.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.1.2.1. Pro: There were [many](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_historical_acts_of_tax_resistance#21st_Century) protests against taxation in 2018, including major protests in [Jordan](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2018/12/jordan-anti-tax-protests-resume-government-seeks-dialogue-181214071233264.html) and [Bulgaria](https://in.reuters.com/article/bulgaria-protests/thousands-protest-in-bulgaria-against-high-fuel-prices-car-taxes-idINKCN1NG0P1).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.1.2.2. Pro: There have been [protests against taxes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poll_tax_riots) in the UK.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.1.3. Pro: Any similar protests in the UK would be stronger, because they would be protesting a specific failure to listen to clearly voted upon issue \(the referendum\) rather than a general economic protest about high taxes.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.2. Pro: MPs [have](https://www.telegraph.co.uk/politics/2019/02/26/delaying-brexit-risks-surge-right-wing-extremism-warns-jacob/) [warned](https://www.express.co.uk/news/uk/1097228/Brexit-news-UK-EU-Theresa-May-deal-European-Union-vote-Commons) that delays to Brexit will cause significant anger amongst the public.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.2.1. Con: Brexit has been [delayed](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-47889404). There has been no related violence.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.3. Con: MP's have the responsibility to act in the best interests of the country as they see those interests, not to accede to threats of civil disobedience.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.3.1. Pro: [73.8%](http://home.bt.com/news/uk-news/how-mps-voted-in-the-eu-referendum-11364110245462) of MPs voted Remain.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.4. Con: A no-deal Brexit will likely lead to violence as well.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.4.1. Pro: [Supermarkets](https://inews.co.uk/news/brexit/no-deal-brexit-supermarket-food-shortages-looting-preparations/) are preparing for looting and riots as a result of food shortages following a no-deal Brexit.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.4.2. Pro: The [Government](https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/plan-to-evacuate-the-queen-after-a-no-deal-brexit-35hft7ctw) has updated emergency evacuation plans in preperation for a no-deal scenario.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.4.3. Pro: According to an EU source secret [EU reporting says](https://metro.co.uk/2019/01/28/riots-will-hit-streets-brexit-uk-will-unstable-years-eu-report-warns-8404836/) 'violence is almost inevitable no matter what.' 'They are worried that if the current deal goes through the right-wing will kick off. If there’s no deal everybody will object and kick off. If there’s a second referendum, the right will kick off.'
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.4.4. Pro: [Police chiefs](https://news.sky.com/story/police-plan-for-civil-unrest-after-no-deal-brexit-11493685) could be forced to call on the military to tackle civil disorder in the event of a "no-deal" Brexit, according to a leaked document.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.4.5. Pro: The potential impacts as detailed in [Operation Yellowhammer](https://brexitfacts.blog.gov.uk/2019/09/12/yellowhammer-factsheet/?gclid=CjwKCAjwwvfrBRBIEiwA2nFiPTedUTT50fCl1GpmdJvKVEl1AXqZw113i_kzJE9phRDf9CXZYtKvyxoCCuEQAvD_BwE) are far more likely, as the government's own analysis makes clear, to lead to civil unrest and disobedience.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.4.5.1. Pro: The [government's presentation](https://inews.co.uk/news/brexit/operation-yellowhammer-no-deal-brexit-report-base-case-reasonable-worst-title/) of a base case scenario as "reasonable worst case" is likely to lead to fury if no deal is enacted and the warnings come to pass.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.5. Con: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.6.4.5.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.7. Pro: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.4.13.2.1.10.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.8. Con: Even just trying to leave the EU has brought down [two](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2016/jun/24/david-cameron-resigns-after-uk-votes-to-leave-european-union) [governments](https://www.bbc.com/news/election-2017-46225949), and may in fact be about to [destroy the two-party system](https://theweek.com/articles/817787/how-britain-ends) which had carried on for a century. That's pretty [unstable](https://www.abc.net.au/news/2018-11-19/brexit-could-spell-the-end-of-the-united-kingdom/10510052).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.8.1. Pro: The process has already been the downfall of two Prime Ministers.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9. Con: The UK leaving the EU politically harms the EU and wider Europe.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.1. Con: The harming of the EU will provide impetus for the EU to offer a better deal to encourage the UK to rejoin.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.1.1. Con: The UK hasn't left yet, so it can't rejoin. If the UK were to seek to rejoin after it left, it would likely mean having to sign up to schengen, euro and EU army, arguably a worse position than it currently enjoys.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.1.2. Con: The terms for the UK to rejoin the EU are likely to be worse than those it already has as a full member.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2. Pro: Brexit strengthens [Eurosceptic parties](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jun/24/european-far-right-hails-britains-brexit-vote-marine-le-pen) throughout Europe \(making other exit votes more likely\), posing an existential threat to the EU.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.1. Pro: EU politicians [fear](http://www.cer.eu/insights/impact-brexit-eu) the greater German dominance that will emerge without the UK's check on German will.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.1.1. Pro: Poland saw Brexit as negative, largely because the UK acted as a [counterweight](https://www.politico.eu/article/poland-mourns-brexit/) to the eurozone countries \(particularly Germany\) and therefore aligned with its interests.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.2. Con: [Approval](https://qz.com/1153966/britain-rejected-the-eu-and-the-eu-is-loving-its-new-life/) of the EU has gone up amongst the citizens of Germany, Hungary, Sweden, the Netherlands, Spain, Italy and France since the referendum.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.2.1. Pro: Even Italy's eurosceptic 5-Star Movement, which leads opinion polls ahead of the upcoming election, has [abandoned](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-italy-election-5star/italys-5-star-presents-election-program-with-no-euro-referendum-idUSKBN1FB1LM) its plans for a referendum on membership in the eurozone.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.2.2. Con: Brexit, as a symbol of a populist uprising agains the globalist order, has emboldened actors \(such as Hungarian Prime Minister [Viktor Orbán](https://news.vice.com/en_us/article/a3jmba/trumps-victory-and-brexit-have-emboldened-hungarys-prime-minister-to-lead-a-populist-revolt-in-europe)\) who, while not wanting to leave the EU, seek to [undermine](http://www.theneweuropean.co.uk/top-stories/viktor-orban-enemy-within-1-5300076) it.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.2.2.1. Con: Orbán is the democratically elected and extremely popular prime minister of Hungary and should not be glibly maligned.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.2.3. Pro: [Eurobarometer 88](http://ec.europa.eu/commfrontoffice/publicopinion/index.cfm/Survey/getSurveyDetail/instruments/STANDARD/surveyKy/2143) \(p. 15\) confirms an improving overall image of the EU since the Brexit referendum in 2016.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.3. Con: The UK's fall from the fastest growing member of the G7 to the [slowest](https://uk.reuters.com/article/us-britain-economy/uk-economy-lags-behind-g7-after-2017-growth-rate-cut-idUKKCN1G6110) will serve as a warning to other countries as to the effect of leaving the EU.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.3.1. Con: The citizens of other countries aren’t stupid enough to look at short term economic blips but rather longer term trends.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.3.2. Con: This only applies if Brexit is extremely harmful for the UK economy in the long term, a point which is [heavily contested](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2017/dec/07/brexit-success-story-leaders-lost-plot-uk).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.3.2.1. Con: The short term harm to the economy can also serve as a signal to the remaining members of the EU to not arrange for a referendum, especially as a short term economic hit would be attributed to the ruling party in question.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.3. Con: The EU will feel a greater sense of [cohesiveness](https://www.thebalance.com/brexit-consequences-4062999) without the UK holding it back on key issues.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.3.1. Pro: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.2.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.3.2. Con: EU's cohesion policy is in under threat due to economic and financial effects of Brexit. [Budget consequences article.](https://www.politico.eu/article/commission-gets-glimpse-of-post-brexit-eu-budget-horrors/) [Report on cohesion policy challenges in the light of Brexit.](http://eprints.lse.ac.uk/83499/1/Begg_Cohesion%20policy_2017.pdf)
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.3.3. Pro: EU officials think [greater integration](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-eu-future-timmermans/germany-and-france-to-lead-post-brexit-eu-in-further-integration-idUSKBN19I14O) will be possible without the UK's opposition.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.3.3.1. Pro: The UK's special EU Reform deal would have included exemption from the "[Ever Closer Union](https://fullfact.org/europe/explaining-eu-deal-ever-closer-union/)" of the EU.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.3.4. Con: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.2.2.2.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.4. Con: The UK has no obligation to the EU, and should only do what is in its interests. The harms to the EU of Brexit are irrelevant.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.4.1. Con: If the UK leaving the EU harms the lives of millions of people in Europe, this is a relevant factor in the decision at a moral level.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.4.1.1. Pro: Even in terms of national interest, acting immorally by harming the lives of European citizens also has a negative consequence of harming the UK's relations and public image.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.4.2. Con: This debate is not inherently from the UK's perspective. It is unclear why we should not also factor in the benefit of hundreds of millions of people in Europe.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.4.3. Con: Whether within or outside of the EU the UK needs to take the interests of its closest allies \(the EU member states\) into account for its foreign policy. This is because they share many geopolitical interests which are less likely to be promoted with a weakened EU.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.4.4. Con: The harms to the EU can lead to economical, political or other crises which can spread beyond the EU borders.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5. Pro: A hard Brexit makes the expansion of the EU more [challenging.](https://www.ft.com/content/2cd87b08-42ac-11e6-b22f-79eb4891c97d)
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.1. Pro: The UK has long been a [vocal proponent of extending](https://www.ft.com/content/2cd87b08-42ac-11e6-b22f-79eb4891c97d) the bloc into ex-communist central and eastern Europe. Other donor states will become less willing and able to support this without the support and funding of the UK.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.1.1. Con: Germany, not the UK, has taken the lead on many accession talks [since 2014](http://country.eiu.com/article.aspx?articleid=1014763485&Country=Albania&topic=Politics&subtopic=Forecast&subsubtopic=International+relations).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2. Con: EU expansion is bad for Europe and bad for accession states.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.1. Con: Growth potential in accession states like [Serbia](https://www.weforum.org/agenda/2016/01/the-future-of-serbia-s-economy/) and [Ukraine](https://www.ft.com/content/9d2173a2-60d7-11e7-8814-0ac7eb84e5f1) is high. They could be strong trade partners for the EU \(and the UK if they stay\).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.2. Con: The influence of Russia in the [Balkans](http://www.lse.ac.uk/LSEE-Research-on-South-Eastern-Europe/Assets/Documents/Events/Conferences-Symposia-Programmes-and-Agendas/2015-Report-Russia-in-the-Balkans-merged-document.pdf) and [Ukraine](http://theweek.com/articles/449691/ukraines-fraught-relationship-russia-brief-history) is troublesome for the UK and the EU. Russia constitutes an [attractive model](https://freedomhouse.org/report/special-reports/ever-farther-union-balkans-and-brexit) of government for a number of regional leaders, who might seek to align their policies more with Russia and other non-EU actors. If these states are not brought into the EU fold they may fall back under the influence of Russia which is not in the UK or EU's interest geopolitically.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.3. Con: Prospects of EU accession have long been drivers of reforms preventing ethnic conflict and discrimination. Political analysts and diplomats worry that the loss of EU leverage in accession states could pose a [security threat](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-europe-cee-integration/central-european-states-urge-eu-to-speed-up-enlargement-in-west-balkans-idUSKBN19V1FT) for entire European community.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.4. Pro: As [Greece](https://www.economist.com/news/leaders/21724810-country-saves-too-much-and-spends-too-little-why-germanys-current-account-surplus-bad) demonstrated, some states in the EU cannot compete with the larger and more developed economies of Western Europe. This leads to loss of industry, jobs, and forces the countries to run government deficits to offset trade imbalances.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.4.1. Pro: -> See 1.8.4.2.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.5. Pro: As we see with [Hungary](http://carnegieeurope.eu/2017/09/04/defending-eu-values-in-poland-and-hungary-pub-72988), some states have competing values to the EU and once added foment internal conflict and a crisis of common values.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.5.1. Pro: -> See discussion #19119: Hungary should leave the European Union.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.5.2. Con: -> See 1.4.3.7.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.5.3. Pro: -> See 1.4.3.7.2.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.5.4. Pro: Turkey, run by what is considered to be an [authoritarian regime](https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2016/07/how-erdogan-made-turkey-authoritarian-again/492374/) by many, is one of the states that has been considered historically in accession debates. Its competing values upon admission would certainly call the EU's values into question.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.5.4.1. Con: -> See 1.6.3.4.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.6. Pro: New member states tend to put economic strains on the funds of the union as we have [seen in the past](http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/talking_point/2565277.stm). This not only puts economic strain on the union, but reduces the available structural funding for current EU recipients.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.7. Con: The EU is [based on](https://europa.eu/european-union/topics/human-rights_en) “freedom, democracy, equality, the rule of law and respect for human rights.” This is universal and does not just apply to original member states. Once they meet democratic and economic criteria, the EU has a moral obligation to let accession states in.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.8. Con: Adding new members to the EU like Ukraine and states in the Western Balkans gives it strength in numbers and increased leverage on a global stage as a bloc.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.3. Pro: Brexit makes states deciding to join the EU more [uncertain](https://freedomhouse.org/report/special-reports/ever-farther-union-balkans-and-brexit) about its future and thus [less likely](https://www.voanews.com/a/brexit-dampens-zeal-for-serbias-eu-bid/3407552.html) to join.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.3.1. Con: The accession process is likely to remain a foreign policy priority for all western Balkan countries because these states do not have a [viable economic alternative](http://country.eiu.com/article.aspx?articleid=1014763485&Country=Albania&topic=Politics&subtopic=Forecast&subsubtopic=International+relations).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.3.1.1. Con: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.5.2.2.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6. Pro: Brexit will harm the economies of EU countries.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.1. Pro: European countries will experience [reduced trade volumes](https://www.politico.eu/article/brexit-impact-on-european-regions-revealed-by-eu-report-phase-2-negotiations/) because of trade restrictions with the UK.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.2. Pro: The loss of the UK's total contribution to the EU budget leaves a gap to fill of just over [5 percent](https://uk.reuters.com/article/uk-britain-eu-economy-europe/from-trade-to-migration-how-brexit-may-hit-the-eu-economy-idUKKCN0ZA0KE).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.2.1. Pro: This will necessitate cuts in the budget, perhaps causing [development funds](https://www.politico.eu/article/commission-gets-glimpse-of-post-brexit-eu-budget-horrors/) for Western European nations to be scrapped.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.3. Con: A [number of companies](https://www.verdict.co.uk/which-companies-could-leave-the-uk-because-of-brexit/) may relocate to other countries within the EU after the UK leaves.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.4. Pro: The loss of jobs for migrant workers may [harm](https://uk.reuters.com/article/uk-britain-eu-economy-europe/from-trade-to-migration-how-brexit-may-hit-the-eu-economy-idUKKCN0ZA0KE) the economies that currently export workers to the UK.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.4.1. Pro: Migrants working in the UK sent [£1.5 billion to £16.5 billion in Remittances](http://migrationobservatory.ox.ac.uk/resources/briefings/migrant-remittances-to-and-from-the-uk/) to their home countries \(in 2014\).
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.4.2. Con: Skilled migrant workers remaining in their home countries may in fact boost their economies.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.4.2.1. Pro: Poland is [actively attempting](https://www.politico.eu/article/poland-hopes-brexit-will-lead-its-native-stars-home/) to draw skilled young workers back from the UK to benefit the Polish economy.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.4.2.1.1. Con: Poland is the [biggest](http://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-36620886) beneficiary of EU funds, which are transforming the country. The UK leaving means there are less funds for countries like Poland.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.4.3. Con: Other EU developed EU economies, such as France and Germany, may [benefit](https://uk.reuters.com/article/uk-britain-eu-economy-europe/from-trade-to-migration-how-brexit-may-hit-the-eu-economy-idUKKCN0ZA0KE) from an influx of workers who can no longer work in the UK.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.5. Con: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.6.4.2.1.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.7. Pro: Europe faces a world in turmoil. The UK will be weaker outside the EU. This is not the time for Brexit. This is the time to come together and stand up for Europe.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.7.1. Pro: Russian mafia groups are [reported](http://www.dw.com/en/russian-mafia-groups-reportedly-operate-in-europe-on-behalf-of-the-kremlin/a-38617828) to be operating in the EU on behalf of the Russian government.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.7.2. Pro: Some criminal gangs in Russia may be [more powerful](https://www.realclearpolitics.com/video/2018/03/16/russian_exile_mikhail_khodorkovsky_a_criminal_gang_runs_the_kremlin_putin_may_no_longer_be_main_boss.html) than the government itself, and thus represent an even greater risk for the stability of Europe.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.7.3. Pro: The political turmoil in the United States is [destabilising](https://www.irishtimes.com/business/markets/us-political-turmoil-sends-shockwave-through-global-markets-1.3312843) the stock market in European countries.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.9.7.4. Pro: The United States Trump government [may be corrupt](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/us-politics/donald-trump-white-house-howard-dean-vermont-governor-criminal-democratic-dnc-chair-a8130396.html), which means it is perhaps a less useful and less reliable ally for Europe.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.10. Con: Leaving the EU is a project that is so all-encompassing that it will dominate the activities of the British government for years to come. Therefore without a majority-supported clear course of action, Brexit is unsustainable in the long term, and even in the short term.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.10.1. Pro: The much needed [adults' social care green paper](https://researchbriefings.parliament.uk/ResearchBriefing/Summary/CBP-8002) continues to be further delayed due to civil servant distraction with brexit issues.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.11. Con: By remaining in the EU, the UK would be able to operate broadly as before but with clear caveats regarding some issues that concern its citizens.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.12. Pro: Deciding to remain in the EU grants UKIP a new and powerful antiestablishment narrative of betrayal.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.12.1. Con: Nigel Farage [has already made comments contradicting himself on the economic benefits of Brexit.](https://twitter.com/open_britain/status/1002472366629322752) It will also be possible to present an equally powerful narrative of UKIP as being con-artists and betrayers.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.12.2. Pro: UKIP is immensely culturally divisive. Past leaders such as Nigel Farage have made racist, sexist, and xenophobic [comments](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/nigel-farage-resigns-ukip-leader-brexit-leave-most-controversial-moments-racism-sexism-immigration-a7118801.html). Current UKIP leader Henry Bolton has [stated](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2017/sep/11/leadership-hopeful-warns-wrong-leader-could-turn-ukip-into-uks-nazi-party-henry-bolton) that under the wrong leadership, UKIP risks becoming the "UK Nazi Party."
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.12.2.1. Pro: UKIP has close [ties](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2014/mar/10/ukip-faces-questions-far-right-europe-for-freedom-and-democracy) to extreme far-right, anti-Islam parties in Europe, such as the Italian Lega Nord.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.12.2.2. Pro: When addressing issues such as immigration, UKIP [chooses](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/politics/ukip/10782059/Nigel-Farage-takes-his-message-to-the-country.html) to frame the debate as a struggle between the "Westminster elite" and the rest of Britain, rather than engaging in substantive debate on whatever the issue is at hand. This makes productive discourse around such matters more difficult.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.12.3. Pro: UKIP was accused of inciting racial [hatred](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2016/jun/16/nigel-farage-defends-ukip-breaking-point-poster-queue-of-migrants) with its controversial "breaking point" posters.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.12.4. Pro: As they [considered](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2014/nov/19/two-tory-mps-defect-ukip-wins-rochester-reckless) in 2014, the newly empowered UKIP will lure in many disaffected Tories, making it difficult to form a majority government.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.12.5. Con: Leaving the EU to just to appease Ukip sympathisers is giving in to ransom. Historically this validates and strengthens their overall narrative. People who disagree with their narrative \(on betrayal by the establishment, or anything else\) should challenge, rather than condone, it.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.12.6. Con: The UKIP vote has [collapsed](https://www.politico.eu/article/uk-general-election-ukip-why-collapse-matters-conservative-majority-theresa-may/), and three leadership elections since the referendum have [strained](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2018/jan/21/ukip-leader-henry-bolton-says-party-could-collapse-if-it-ousted-him) the party's budget.  It is unlikely the party in its current form can regain the type of power it held before 2016.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.12.7. Pro: Immigration was less of an [issue](http://www.electionanalysis.uk/uk-election-analysis-2017/section-4-parties-and-the-campaign/why-immigration-faded-from-view-in-election-2017/) in election 2017 than it had been prior to the referendum. This was in part because many Leave supporters believed a Brexit deal would alleviate their concerns about immigration. Staying in the EU will rekindle the divisive politics of the referendum, as these betrayed voters would be drawn back to antiestablishment parties such as UKIP.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.13. Con: Opinion polls indicate that the public regrets the Brexit vote. A [YouGov survey](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2017/oct/13/labour-flags-up-brexit-poll-which-suggests-public-regret-decision), this past October, found that only 42% of respondents think it is right to leave the EU, compared with 47% who think it is wrong. This is a shift since the referendum.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.13.1. Pro: Out of that 42% who still think it is right to leave the EU, not all of them would support a Hard Brexit.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.13.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.4.13.2.1.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.14. Pro: If Britain wants to trade with the EU, it will still be forced to follow EU trade regulations, but without any input on what those regulations are.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.14.1. Pro: It is usually more costly for a company to produce different versions of the same product to satisfy the rules of different export markets. This will mean that, on average, manufacturers wishing to export to the EU will have to produce their products to EU standards as a minimum. As a result, there will be no option for those companies but to follow EU standards and regulations even if the UK decides to change those rules.
1.10.1.4.1.4.3.14.2. Con: Only companies trading with EU will have to follow these regulations and only specific regulations will be applied. The UK is trading with the US but not all US regulations are part of the law in the UK.
1.10.1.4.2. Pro: In the UK, [32%](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/election-2017-40192060) of MPs are women, whereas in the EU [37.4%](http://www.europarl.europa.eu/RegData/publications/2017/0001/P8_PUB%282017%290001_EN.pdf) of MEPs are women.
1.10.1.4.3. Pro: The UKs unadjusted Gender pay gap is [21%](http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/index.php/Gender_pay_gap_statistics).
1.10.1.4.3.1. Pro: The UKs Gender pay gap is the 4th largest in the EU, and is [higher than](http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/index.php/Gender_pay_gap_statistics) the EU member state average by 4.8%.
1.10.1.4.3.2. Con: Much of the purported gender pay gap is actually [due to part time work being less well paid \(per hour\) than full time work](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/magazine-37198653), and women being disproportionately more likely to do part time work.
1.10.1.4.3.3. Pro: It would be hypocritical to leave the EU citing sexism as a reason.
1.10.1.4.4. Pro: Gender inequality is a global problem, as measured by the UNDPs [Gender Inequality Index](http://hdr.undp.org/en/content/gender-inequality-index-gii).
1.10.1.5. Con: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.
1.10.1.6. Con: MEP selection is made by the party being voted for by the electorate as elections are conducted using the proportional representation system. This means if someone votes for Labour, for example, the Labour Party allocates the candidate. Lack of diversity is therefore down to who the parties put up, rather than the EU as an organisation.
1.10.1.7. Con: Ethnic diversity doesn't just include different skin colours. There are at least 28 \(but undoubtedly more\) different ethnicities in the Commission and Parliament.
1.10.1.8. Con: Positive Discrimination Targets as inherently demanded in the question are in general not a healthy way to target discrimination - as they are necessarily discriminatory themselves. Equality of opportunity, not of outcome, should be the goal. This is the path to a meritocracy.
1.10.1.9. Con: [8%](https://researchbriefings.parliament.uk/ResearchBriefing/Summary/SN01156) of MPs are from ethnic minority backgrounds, compared to 13% of the general population. The UK itself lacks diversity in representation.
1.10.2. Con: The EU has been a driver of equality policy in Europe.
1.10.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.4.6.1.
1.10.2.2. Pro: The UK has introduced many of its equality measures as a result of EU initiatives.
1.10.2.2.1. Pro: The Equality Act 2010 is the piece of UK legislation which protects people in the workplace and wider society from discrimination on various grounds \(including age, disability, race and sexual orientation\). It [implements four major EU Equal Treatment Directives](https://rightsinfo.org/10-times-european-union-made-difference-human-rights/).
1.10.2.2.1.1. Con: The UK may have created the same rules as the four "Equal Treatment Directives" by themselves, if the EU had not made them first.
1.10.2.2.2. Con: The UK is heavily represented at the EU, and played a key role in the drafting of these equality measures. In the vast majority of cases, the UK would likely have drawn up similar protections had it been outside the EU.
1.10.2.2.2.1. Con: Whilst the British Government seeks to replicate most EU laws for ease of trading, it refuses to protect EU laws on human rights, offering '[basic rights](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/brexit-mps-vote-against-including-european-fundamental-rights-charter-in-uk-law-a8162981.html)' instead.
1.10.2.2.3. Pro: The British [Equality and Human Rights Commission](https://www.equalityhumanrights.com/en/about-us/who-we-are) claims that [EU law has led to changes in UK law](https://www.equalityhumanrights.com/en/our-human-rights-work/what-does-brexit-mean-equality-and-human-rights-uk), which protect equality and human rights. These include data protection, human trafficking, disability rights, workplace discrimination, and equal pay.
1.10.2.3. Pro: -> See 1.4.6.1.1.
1.10.2.4. Con: The UK consistently has the lowest rates of discrimination across the EU, showing that it is not the EU per se that should take credit for high equality, but rather British governments, courts and society in general. See e.g. [figure 5 here](http://fra.europa.eu/sites/default/files/fra_uploads/fra-2017-eu-midis-ii-main-results_en.pdf)
1.10.2.5. Con: It is the [UK that has been a driver](https://www.politico.eu/article/brexit-diversity-exits-the-eu-brussels/) of equality policy in the EU, not the reverse.
1.10.2.6. Pro: The UK has strong equality policies.  By being part of a larger community it can push those policies even further, to affect more people.
1.10.2.6.1. Con: The UK can lead by example just as effectively, if not more effectively, outside the EU where it is not seeking to impose laws on other countries.
1.10.2.6.2. Con: Even if it were true that the UK wants to push equality policies further, and given the [backlash against political correctness](https://www.express.co.uk/comment/columnists/martin-townsend/772180/trevor-phillips-political-correctness-documentary-channel-4-gone-mad) this is unsubstantiated, it is not at all clear that the UK should seek to legally impose those policies on other countries.
1.10.3. Con: The EU commissions senior management is [35% female](http://europa.eu/rapid/press-release_IP-17-4778_en.htm), and 37% of middle management is female.
1.10.3.1. Con: -> See 1.10.1.2.
1.10.3.2. Pro: The EU launched a new “[Diversity and Inclusion Charter](https://www.eubusiness.com/topics/employment/diversity-inclusion/)” in 2017 with promises of fresh action to reach at least 40 per cent women in its management by Nov 1, 2019.
1.10.3.3. Pro: This is [higher than](http://www.cityam.com/260427/number-uk-senior-business-roles-held-women-has-fallen-says) the UKs \(falling\) average of 19% in senior roles, and the global average of 25%.
1.10.3.3.1. Con: Comparing the EU bureaucracy to private companies is inappropriate.
1.10.3.3.1.1. Pro: The EU bureaucracy passes and upholds laws on gender equality, and so should be expected to "practice what it preaches" and achieve higher gender equality than private companies do.
1.10.3.3.2. Con: The UK’s civil service has [40% women](https://www.instituteforgovernment.org.uk/blog/civil-service-gender-balance-2016) in the most senior roles and over 45% in the next most senior roles.
1.10.3.4. Con: -> See 1.10.3.3.2.
1.10.3.5. Pro: This is higher than the worldwide average for parliaments \([22.8% as of June 2016](http://www.unwomen.org/en/what-we-do/leadership-and-political-participation/facts-and-figures)\).
1.10.3.6. Pro: This is higher than the Fortune 500 average of Female Senior managers \([20.5%](http://fortune.com/2017/06/09/white-men-senior-executives-fortune-500-companies-diversity-data/)\).
1.10.3.6.1. Con: -> See 1.10.3.3.1.
1.10.4. Pro: The European Council \(made up of the leaders of the 28 EU member states\) is just 10% female \(UK, Germany, Lithuania\), whereas the UK cabinet is much more progressive with [30% female members](https://www.gov.uk/government/ministers).
1.10.4.1. Con: The EU parliament, with [37% female MEPs](https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&source=web&rct=j&url=http://www.europarl.europa.eu/RegData/publications/2017/0001/P8_PUB%25282017%25290001_EN.pdf&ved=2ahUKEwi839LO26rhAhVTURUIHSOGCHIQFjABegQIBxAF&usg=AOvVaw1wO3RKXF0wohqUqYJmc5Zg&cshid=1553978160967), is more progressive than the house of commons, with only [32% female MPs](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_the_House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom).
1.10.4.1.1. Pro: The Conservative party, the biggest single group in the house of commons, has the lowest female representation of all parties excepting the DUP.
1.10.4.2. Con: Both are far from exemplars of progressivism, with a lower ratio of women in leadership positions than in backbench positions-- [EU](https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&source=web&rct=j&url=http://www.europarl.europa.eu/RegData/publications/2017/0001/P8_PUB%25282017%25290001_EN.pdf&ved=2ahUKEwi839LO26rhAhVTURUIHSOGCHIQFjABegQIBxAF&usg=AOvVaw1wO3RKXF0wohqUqYJmc5Zg&cshid=1553978344485) / [UK](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_the_House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom)
1.11. Con: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.13.5.
1.12. Pro: -> See 1.10.1.4.1.4.3.
